              <span id="reviewTextContainer165494207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5910297376887839259">This book was a very quick read, due to the fact that I didn't want to stop reading it. Todd Burpo did an excellent job in describing the events that led to his son's discovery of Heaven. If you have children, you can appreciate his depiction of the events and mannerisms of his children. If you have lost a child, you can appreciate the pain that Todd, and especially his wife reflect upon, and the sheer joy that they experience when they are delivered a simple, yet powerful message from their son</span>
  <span id="freeText5910297376887839259" style="display:none">This book was a very quick read, due to the fact that I didn't want to stop reading it. Todd Burpo did an excellent job in describing the events that led to his son's discovery of Heaven. If you have children, you can appreciate his depiction of the events and mannerisms of his children. If you have lost a child, you can appreciate the pain that Todd, and especially his wife reflect upon, and the sheer joy that they experience when they are delivered a simple, yet powerful message from their son, Colton.<br /><br />Although I didn't want to put this book down, I would have to stop reading for at least a few minutes between chapters, as I had to take that time to reflect upon what I had just read.<br /><br />Having grown up a Catholic, I truly believe in Heaven and always have.... but this book turns that belief into a form of peace that I never knew was missing.<br /><br />This is a crazy, wild-kind-of-ride world that we live in, and if you are a believer in Heaven (or not) this is a book that will settle you down and place your faith in its proper perspective.... at least that's what it did for me.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_157277655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157277655" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93350-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389209461p2/93350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157277655?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/93350-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157277655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14900249161762827380">Why did I read this book? I don't know. I saw the family on the Today Show, and they seemed honest and earnest and pretty normal. When something extraordinary happens to regular people, I tend to be more open to believe it. So if this little boy was claiming he visited heaven, I was curious to see what he had to say about it. <br/><br/>In short, the Burpo family's 4 year-old son Colton suffers from a burst appendix and nearly dies on the operating table. I won't go into discussing why the family waited wh</span>
  <span id="freeText14900249161762827380" style="display:none">Why did I read this book? I don't know. I saw the family on the Today Show, and they seemed honest and earnest and pretty normal. When something extraordinary happens to regular people, I tend to be more open to believe it. So if this little boy was claiming he visited heaven, I was curious to see what he had to say about it. <br /><br />In short, the Burpo family's 4 year-old son Colton suffers from a burst appendix and nearly dies on the operating table. I won't go into discussing why the family waited what seemed far too long to go to a hospital, nor will I debate the obvious ineptness encountered at the small-town local hospital who misdiagnosed Colton 's condition and nearly killed him. When Colton finally receives medical care from professionals who seem to have done more than play "Operation" and watch "ER," he has a near-death experience on the operating table, sees his parents as he floats up and out of his body (in separate rooms, his pastor father praying, his mother on her cell phone--which he couldn't have known and they claim to be true) and visits heaven. <br /><br />This is where things started to go horribly wrong for me. Colton's version of heaven is pretty much what I would expect from a 4 year old with a pastor for a dad-- everyone in heaven is wearing white robes (with colored sashes), the angels have wings, the colors are bright, everyone is nice, Jesus still has the wounds from his crucifixion ("markers" Colton called it), there are lots of children and animals and the gates to heaven are made up of gold and pearls. But Colton's dad, the Pastor Todd Burpo, claims at every turn these descriptions <i>must</i> be true because Colton wouldn't have known that! How could he describe these things when he's never been exposed to them? A four-year old wouldn't have known those things! Really? You expect me to believe that a four-year-old with a pastor for a dad, who spends a lot of time in a church, and whose mother is the Sunday school teacher was never exposed to images of angels, people in white robes, the "pearly gates" or a depiction of the Crucifixion? Strike one.<br /><br />The Burpos played it cool on the Today Show. No talk of the consequences of not accepting Jesus as your personal savior. Shrewd marketing move. So the constant proselytizing throughout the book was somewhat of a surprise to me. I guess I'm just a naive quasi-Jew/wavering-agnostic-atheist. The book is rife with beating the drum about accepting Jesus into your heart or you won't get into heaven. Colton returns from his trip to heaven bursting with this information, to the point that he almost disrupts someone's funeral service by loudly demanding to know if the deceased had accepted Christ into his heart. I find this behavior in a little kid to be horrifying. It reeks of brainwashing and intolerance. Colton's version of heaven didn't allow for any other religions? No Jews, Muslims, Buddhists, Hindus-- nevermind the ancient Greeks, Romans, Egyptians and so on? I guess heaven didn't exist before the time of Christ? Or maybe Dante is right and all us heathen unbaptized are hanging out on a lower ring of limbo/hell together, either because we had the misfortune of being born before the time of Christ, or being too foolish to accept the Truth? Strike two.<br /><br />The Burpos extracted the information from Colton over several years before they decided to start keeping notes. Colton said he met his sister, who his parents confirmed was miscarried at 2 months(obviously, they didn't know it was a sister at the time). This was intriguing, as I do believe Colton had no idea his mom had had a miscarriage. But he also claims to have met lots of children in heaven-- but neither Todd nor his wife thought it would be interesting to write down any of these children's names just to see? Am I just too skeptical? If someone told you they went to heaven and met so-and-so, wouldn't you want to look that person up? To verify? I guess this is where the concept of "faith" and the concept of "logic" start to war it out in my mind. In any case, strike three.<br /><br />I wanted to like this book. I wanted to have an open mind and try to see the value in other points of view and maybe gain an understanding into faith and perhaps some validity in the supernatural. But I just couldn't. <br /><br />I guess I'll see you in Hell.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14900249161762827380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156480146" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156480146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10061433686020569892">I don't doubt for a minute that this kid believes what he is saying. After all, he was 4 when it happened. Aside from heaven being real, I'm guessing he believes many other things are real too: Elmo, Mickey Mouse, and unicorns. What I can't fathom is that his parents would be gullible enough to believe it too. Although, the fact that when Todd says "as a pastor, I'm not a believer in superstition" he doesn't see the irony in the statement, it should have told me everything I needed to know about</span>
  <span id="freeText10061433686020569892" style="display:none">I don't doubt for a minute that this kid believes what he is saying. After all, he was 4 when it happened. Aside from heaven being real, I'm guessing he believes many other things are real too: Elmo, Mickey Mouse, and unicorns. What I can't fathom is that his parents would be gullible enough to believe it too. Although, the fact that when Todd says "as a pastor, I'm not a believer in superstition" he doesn't see the irony in the statement, it should have told me everything I needed to know about him. Of course, it could be true. I mean, how couldn't a story created by a four year old pastor's son, one that was added to and embellished over the course of several years, one that described jesus exactly as you have seen him painted on a million pieces of black velvet, one that was fitted into scripture by the author, not be true?<p>At any rate, if you believe in this sort of thing, you'll probably find this story inspirational. If you don't you will most likely find this story laughable and pathetic.</p><p>So Todd, now that you have a bestseller and your benevolent God has rewarded you with a wad of cash, have fun trying to fit through the eye of that needle on the way to heaven.</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12610217193422987628">Heaven Is for Real: A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back, Todd Burpo, Lynn Vincent<br/>Heaven is for Real: A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back is a 2010 Christian book written by Todd Burpo and Lynn Vincen. The book documents the report of a near-death experience by Burpo's three-year-old son Colton. Todd Burpo and Lynn Vincent co-wrote this book when Todd Burpo’s three-year-old son had appendicitis. When Colton’s mother, Sonja, first noticed he wa</span>
  <span id="freeText12610217193422987628" style="display:none">Heaven Is for Real: A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back, Todd Burpo, Lynn Vincent<br />Heaven is for Real: A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back is a 2010 Christian book written by Todd Burpo and Lynn Vincen. The book documents the report of a near-death experience by Burpo's three-year-old son Colton. Todd Burpo and Lynn Vincent co-wrote this book when Todd Burpo’s three-year-old son had appendicitis. When Colton’s mother, Sonja, first noticed he was not feeling well she took him to the emergency room, and was told that Colton had influenza, as all the tests for a possible appendicitis came back negative. As time passed on, Colton continuously kept throwing up, which is when Todd and Sonja knew that he did not just have influenza. When Todd and Sonja went to a different emergency room with Colton, they were told that Colton had to have an emergency appendectomy as he could possibly die. Months after surviving the emergency surgery to remove his appendix, Colton shared the story of how he left his body, during surgery, and went to heaven. Colton began describing events, and people that seemed impossible for him to have known about. Examples include knowledge of an unborn sister miscarried by his mother in 1998 and details of a great-grandfather who had died 30 years before Colton was born. Colton also explained how he met Jesus riding a rainbow-colored horse, and sat in Jesus' lap while angels sang songs to him. He also saw Mary kneeling before the throne of God, and at other times standing beside Jesus.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفدهم ماه می سال 2019 میلادی<br />عنوان: بهشت واقعی است؛ نویسندگان: تاد بورپو؛ لین وینسنت؛ مترجم: پروین دانشور؛ تهران: منشور آذین، ‏‫1396؛ در 262 ص؛ شابک: 9786009863822؛‬ عنوان دیگر: عنوان دیگر: بهشت واقعی است: داستان شگفت‌ انگیز یک کودک از سفر به بهشت و بازگشت از آن؛ موضوع: تجربه های دم مرگ - بهشت مسیحیت - از نویسندگان ایالات متحده آمریکا - سده 20 م<br /><br />در کتاب «بهشت واقعی است» تاد بارپو (بورپو)، کشیش کلیسای «وسلیان» در «نبراسکای امریکا» چنین می‌نویسد، که پسر چهارساله‌ اش، «کلتون»، ماه‌ها پس از عمل جراحی، در سال 2003 میلادی، به بازگویی رخدادها و افرادی کرده است، که داشتن شناخت از آنها، برای او ناممکن بوده است. برای مثال پسربچه، از خواهری که هنوز به دنیا نیامده است، حرف می‌زند، اما پدر و مادر، هنوز درباره ی این موضوع، برای او چیزی بازگو نکرده‌ اند. پسربچه پدر بزرگی را توصیف می‌کند،که سی سال پیش از تولد او درگذشته است. «کلتون» همچنین ادعا می‌کند، که شخصا با حضرت عیسی مسیح، ملاقات کرده، و در حالیکه فرشته‌ها برایش آواز می‌خوانده‌ اند، با او سوار اسب شده است. او همچنین گفته که در بهشت حضرت مریم را دیده، که در محضر خدا زانو زده، یا در مواردی دیگر کنار حضرت عیسی ایستاده است. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="12610217193422987628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeni" href="/user/show/1055982-jeni">Jeni</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201534743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14968176022357560815">This book made you think. I feel like it is a feel-good story, and most everything this boy saw went along with what i believe heaven will be. I thought the writing in the beginning was well crafted and the ending wavered a bit, but overall it is a fast, captivating read. It is worth your time. I think it is possible he saw heaven, but I also am not sure all the things his 4 year old said necessarily were accurate, as is the case with all 4 year olds. This book had a way of pulling you in and ma</span>
  <span id="freeText14968176022357560815" style="display:none">This book made you think. I feel like it is a feel-good story, and most everything this boy saw went along with what i believe heaven will be. I thought the writing in the beginning was well crafted and the ending wavered a bit, but overall it is a fast, captivating read. It is worth your time. I think it is possible he saw heaven, but I also am not sure all the things his 4 year old said necessarily were accurate, as is the case with all 4 year olds. This book had a way of pulling you in and making you relate to the journey this average Midwest family took. While reading this book, my own 4-year-old daughter had a dream that Jesus came to our house. She has never told us about her dreams before, ever, and she talked and talked about this dream for days in great detail. I could see how even if this boy didn't go to heaven, he easily could have had a dream, like my daughter, which was very real and life altering for a little boy. It has turned into an interesting way for God to be able to speak to millions of people because it has been a bestseller for months. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14968176022357560815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_229788107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229788107" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2539519-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487050938p2/2539519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229788107?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/2539519-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229788107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9331436050844060451">Heaven may be for real, but the Burpos certainly aren't.<br/><br/>I know it sounds hypocritical for a Christian to be skeptical, but I think in a few years the Burpo family is going to come out and say the whole thing was an elaborate metaphor and they're shocked anyone would take it literally. But thanks for the $$$$.<br/><br/>Overall, the book is a quick, easy read. Sometimes there are too many digressions about how cute the kids are and how awesome small town life is, which seem unnecessary for the scope of the </span>
  <span id="freeText9331436050844060451" style="display:none">Heaven may be for real, but the Burpos certainly aren't.<br /><br />I know it sounds hypocritical for a Christian to be skeptical, but I think in a few years the Burpo family is going to come out and say the whole thing was an elaborate metaphor and they're shocked anyone would take it literally. But thanks for the $$$$.<br /><br />Overall, the book is a quick, easy read. Sometimes there are too many digressions about how cute the kids are and how awesome small town life is, which seem unnecessary for the scope of the book. You know how it is when you don't have kids and you're listening to a friend go on about how awesome their kids are and all you can do is nod and think, "I'm so never going to be that boring" even though you totally are? That's what some passages of this book are like.<br /><br />The spiritual aspect got harder and harder to swallow as the book went on. Sometimes, there are pithy little statements about humility and the way children cut through all the crap adults tell themselves about God. But overall, I just found it increasingly too convenient that a four-year-old who spent three minutes in heaven would manage to cover such an array of topics, from relativity, to the body after death, to the end times. I'm just surprised Colton didn't somehow manage to see creation too.<br /><br />If this was a real kid, wouldn't there be a bunch of statements that don't appear to make any sense? After all, the book of Revelation doesn't make a whole lot of sense. Heaven wouldn't, from our perspective. But Todd seems to leave all these out. <br /><br />What clinched it for me was the description of the final battle, where men fight with swords but women and children have to stand back and watch. Really? We have gender segregation in heaven? It's bad enough that we get our old bodies back, but we conform to conservative 20th century gender ideals? <br /><br />What about that verse that says there is neither male nor female, Jew nor Greek, slave nor free in heaven? Did Todd conveniently forget that one?<br /><br />Read this book so you can discuss it, but on a closer glance Colton's vision of heaven is neither Biblically accurate nor internally consistent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9331436050844060451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172222711" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172222711" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256262-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442983573p2/1256262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172222711?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/1256262-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256262-ron?shelf=christian_life">christian_life</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172222711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13333091513298924700">One sub-genre of Christian literature reports dead-and-back experiences. Because I criticized some as self-serving and frankly false, I receive others for my enlightenment or critique. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7933292.Heaven_is_for_Real_A_Little_Boy_s_Astounding_Story_of_His_Trip_to_Heaven_and_Back' title='Heaven is for Real A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back by Todd Burpo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heaven is for Real: A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back</a> is distinctly different. Naturally, anyone could make up a story about a four-year-old boy's brush with death and his report on what heaven's like. And this <i>may</i> be one of those. I have no way to judge. But unlike so many others of t</span>
  <span id="freeText13333091513298924700" style="display:none">One sub-genre of Christian literature reports dead-and-back experiences. Because I criticized some as self-serving and frankly false, I receive others for my enlightenment or critique. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7933292.Heaven_is_for_Real_A_Little_Boy_s_Astounding_Story_of_His_Trip_to_Heaven_and_Back" title="Heaven is for Real A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back by Todd Burpo" rel="nofollow noopener">Heaven is for Real: A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back</a> is distinctly different. Naturally, anyone could make up a story about a four-year-old boy's brush with death and his report on what heaven's like. And this <i>may</i> be one of those. I have no way to judge. But unlike so many others of the genre—so obviously erroneous based on their own report—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7933292.Heaven_is_for_Real_A_Little_Boy_s_Astounding_Story_of_His_Trip_to_Heaven_and_Back" title="Heaven is for Real A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back by Todd Burpo" rel="nofollow noopener">Heaven is for Real: A Little Boy's Astounding Story of His Trip to Heaven and Back</a> has convincing simplicity and internal integrity while being consistent with the acknowledged reference scriptures.<br /><br />There are weak points, of course. Among the many specific scripture references footnoted, several only have a generic "the scripture says." Unfortunately, those are scriptures with which I am not familiar. It sounds like equivocation. Allowance must also be made for the denominational filter through which Todd and Sonja Burpo experienced and reported, but we've all got filters.<br /><br />The language is folksy and natural, credit I'm sure to Lynn Vincent. (I'm so happy to see competent co-authors come out of the shadows of "ghost writer" to receive the credit they deserve.) The book has a good narrative drama without being melodramatic. The few gaffs—like "like a jib on a sail"—don't detract too much.<br /><br />One of the best of its type.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13333091513298924700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267820910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15968877574269167335"><br/><br/> I love the very last line of the epilogue of this book: "Colton, what do you want people to know from your story?"<br/>(Colton says): " I want them to know that Heaven is for real." <br/>And that's the journey this book took me on. Helping me get a tiny a picture of what Heaven is going to be like. This story also reminded me of the importance of childlike faith, and how much Jesus especially loves children. It emphasized in a new way how important my example and interactions are with the children in my </span>
  <span id="freeText15968877574269167335" style="display:none"><br /><br /> I love the very last line of the epilogue of this book: "Colton, what do you want people to know from your story?"<br />(Colton says): " I want them to know that Heaven is for real." <br />And that's the journey this book took me on. Helping me get a tiny a picture of what Heaven is going to be like. This story also reminded me of the importance of childlike faith, and how much Jesus especially loves children. It emphasized in a new way how important my example and interactions are with the children in my life. Children I work with at my job, and children in my family - Jesus loves them and wants us to show them love. And it's important to really listen to what they have to say as well, because, as was the case with Colton, we as adults have a lot to learn from children.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1414525052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1414525052" />
    <a title="Ross Blocher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10407443-ross-blocher"><img alt="Ross Blocher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340636529p2/10407443.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1414525052?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ross Blocher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ross Blocher" href="/user/show/10407443-ross-blocher">Ross Blocher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1414525052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer278633315407227277">While doing some research on NDEs (near death experiences) at the local library, I noticed the shelf held five copies of "Heaven is for Real" - the story of a boy who went to heaven and came back. (This not to be confused with "The Boy Who Came Back From Heaven", which has now been pulled by the publisher after young Alex Malarkey confessed his story was... fabricated.) It's a bonafide genre now, boasting a number of bestsellers, but "Heaven is for Real" reigns chief amongst them with 10 million</span>
  <span id="freeText278633315407227277" style="display:none">While doing some research on NDEs (near death experiences) at the local library, I noticed the shelf held five copies of "Heaven is for Real" - the story of a boy who went to heaven and came back. (This not to be confused with "The Boy Who Came Back From Heaven", which has now been pulled by the publisher after young Alex Malarkey confessed his story was... fabricated.) It's a bonafide genre now, boasting a number of bestsellers, but "Heaven is for Real" reigns chief amongst them with 10 million copies sold and a successful 2014 film adaptation starring Greg Kinnear.<br /><br />The premise is what you might expect: young Colton Burpo falls ill just short of his 4th birthday with a ruptured appendix, undergoes surgery, and over time his mother and pastor father piece together that Colton had a supernatural visit to heaven in the process.<br /><br />I know what you're thinking: "Enough already! So what does heaven look like?" Well, Jesus is there, and he's really nice, and has beautiful eyes. Colton got to meet Jesus's cousin (John the Baptist). Oh, and Jesus has a rainbow horse. It's never night time, because all the light comes from God and Jesus. And sometimes Satan is there, and Colton won't talk about that. The angels are all carrying swords, because they have to do battle with evil every now and then. They also sing "Jesus Loves Me" and some other Sunday School song I haven't heard of but Colton has. Everybody's got wings, except for Jesus, who moves up and down like an elevator. Jesus sits on the right hand of God, and Gabriel on the left. Mary hangs around, too - she's very proud of Jesus. The Holy Spirit's there, and he's hard to describe, but he's kind of bluish. Lots of animals. Lots of colors. Everybody wears a white robe but a different colored one of these things (sash) and has a glowy thing over their head (halo). Oh, and the kids do homework. They learn things; there's a lot of kids there. Jesus REALLY LOVES THE KIDS. Oh, and Colton was in heaven for three minutes.<br /><br />All makes sense, right? Strangely enough, Colton never died - clinically or otherwise. His vital signs remained solid, though he was under anaesthesia for his surgery. The father, Todd Burpo (the primary author of the book and a pastor) analyzes each description of heaven to find scriptural support. The "Notes" section is just a page and a half of individually-plucked Bible verses. When the elder Burpo does find some loose scriptural connection, he exclaims there's no way his son could have known such esoteric theological tidbits. Todd writes off little inconsistencies, like the fact that haloes are only present in religious art and not part of the biblical descriptions. (Another young girl who has a special "gift" sees lights above the heads of saved people, so they're just aware of something that's not in the Bible.) When Colton says he was in heaven for three minutes, Todd goes into a discussion of how one hour is a thousand years for God. And kids aren't very good with time. Tada! He's impressed that his young son can describe robes and sashes and haloes when he doesn't even know the names for them - and yet, Colton still doesn't know the names for them - he just describes them and lets dad fill in the gaps. Every now and then the father tries to be skeptical and throw his son for a loop, like when he asks Colton what happens in Heaven at night. That's when we learn that there is no night in heaven. Test passed.<br /><br />The real linchpin is that Colton knew his parents were in separate rooms during the surgery, and that mom was on the phone and that dad was praying by himself. Whooooaaaa. He also meets his sister in heaven, who died in mommy's tummy, and no one ever told him that mommy had a miscarriage (the baby had died early enough that no one knew the sex, so now mom and dad are each eager to die first so they can go to heaven and get dibs on naming their long-lost daughter - so sad). He also spends a lot of time with Pop, his dad's maternal grandfather, and no one told Colton his name was "Pop". Colton also doesn't recognize a photo of 60-something Pop, because everyone is young in heaven. Oh, did I forget to mention that? Apparently they're frozen somewhere in their twenties, unless they never reached that age, in which case they're still kids but they continue to grow? I'm confused. But yeah, otherwise they look the same, so too bad if you were hoping to be more gorgeous in heaven. Later on he sees a younger photo and identifies Pop successfully.<br /><br />So yeah, you get the idea. The whole story could have easily been told in half the space, and the remaining pages are filled with unnecessary details about Todd's financial problems and side business selling garage door openers and stuff like that. They brought in Lynn Vincent to help out - the best-selling author of Sarah Palin's memoir - but this still feels like an amateur effort. Some of the aw-shucks writing is painful to read. Heck, this whole thing is painful to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="278633315407227277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I find the book to be another example of why people have difficulty finding any spiritual comfort in religion, </span>

<div id="review_181493051" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181493051" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4302491-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285293021p2/4302491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181493051?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/4302491-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4302491-katie?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4302491-katie?shelf=movie-need-to-see">movie-need-to-see</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181493051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12282282631015497495">**SPOILERS BELOW** <br/><br/>This review may seem a bit negative, but I really didn't think that this book was bad... I just thought it was a little too "stretched" for my liking. I 100% believe that it is possible for this little boy to have gone to heaven & seen Jesus Christ & seen relatives from the other side of the veil. I also believe that it was possible for him to see things that were occurring to his parents while he was in surgery. However, I find a few things that the author talked about a litt</span>
  <span id="freeText12282282631015497495" style="display:none">**SPOILERS BELOW** <br /><br />This review may seem a bit negative, but I really didn't think that this book was bad... I just thought it was a little too "stretched" for my liking. I 100% believe that it is possible for this little boy to have gone to heaven &amp; seen Jesus Christ &amp; seen relatives from the other side of the veil. I also believe that it was possible for him to see things that were occurring to his parents while he was in surgery. However, I find a few things that the author talked about a little hard to swallow. For these reasons, I feel like the author maybe "exaggerated" a little bit - I mean (lets be honest) when we are telling a really compelling story to our friends/family, we all tend to over-embellish details so that our story seems more cutting-edge and gripping for the listener. While I think that this little boy had an INCREDIBLE experience, I feel like there were a lot of details that were a little "too drawn out" which may have helped the author really promote this book. Let me elaborate:<br /><br />1. "Jesus loves the Children" - Any 4 year old boy (or younger) is going to have this engrained in his head growing up. It is going to be something that parents, teachers, family, friends, babysitters, etc. share with children. They share this because they want to teach children about their own faith, they want their children to have a strong conviction of the Savior and live such Christlike principles, and they also share this because of how much it is re-iterated in the Bible. I know and I believe that Jesus loves the children... but just because Colton goes around saying this "non-stop" doesn't necessarily mean that was what the Savior told Colton up there. I believe that the Savior shows others he loves little children through his actions, and while he may have said to Colton that he loved the little children and therefore he loves him... I don't think that the Savior told him that he needed to make sure everyone on earth understood that principle through this little boy.<br /><br />2. "Oh yeah..." I feel like over and over in this book every time the author wanted to teach a religious principle, it was echoed by his son saying, "Oh yeah... I learned that in Heaven." Examples include, "Oh yeah, they do too have swords in heaven.", "Oh yeah, Jesus told me that he told you to personally become a pastor.", "Oh yeah, Jesus told me that if you don't accept him in your heart that you aren't going to heaven.", "Oh yeah, even though you've never told me a story about what Heaven looks like, this is what it looks like.", "Oh yeah, there is going to be a war in heaven." , "Oh yeah, Jesus showed me that you were fighting in it Daddy." "Oh yeah, even though I never met my future brother, I met my so-called, supposed to be sister who appeared the same age as me.", "Oh yeah, Dad didn't you know that God the Father &amp; the Son &amp; the Holy Ghost are three separate beings?" (The list could continue). But the only point that I am trying to make is that all of these topics that Colton supposedly "brought-up on his own" just seems a little to coincidental that they were religious principles that the author was trying to teach the reader. Don't get me wrong, and think that I'm a pessimistic atheist, I actually am a devout Christian - and I believe a lot of the things that were written in this #2 section - but it just seemed a little off to me that the little boy just so happened to have all of these very long conversations with God &amp; Jesus while he was gone &amp; that all the things he talked about fit into this authors "sermon."<br /><br />3. My little boy didn't know the word for... Just because Colton didn't know the word for "sash" &amp; "throne" doesn't mean that he wasn't taught this before hand. He probably was - children learn a lot more through picture books than we give them credit for - so don't act like it was a big revelation that he was teaching you what he saw when in reality, he probably saw it several times before his experience in Heaven.<br /><br />4. Pops &amp; Sister. I believe 100% that you can have experiences with deceased relatives on the other side of the veil - and I believe that Colton was telling the truth when it was explained that he saw his "pops" in his prime age (about 30's). But I have a really hard time believing that he saw his older sister as a sibling typed age - when she was miscarried - it just seems a little back-words and inconsistent with the author's theories... but then again I think that there is a lot we don't know about Heaven &amp; Hell.<br /><br />5. I don't believe for a single second that Colton saw Satan. Really???!!!??? Satan in Heaven... um... that seems like a huge HUGE contradiction to everything that is taught in the Bible. If the author claims that we have to "accept Jesus into our hearts to enter into heaven" then what the crap is Satan doing up in Heaven? And angels with swords guarding heaven so that he can't enter? It seemed a little far-fetched for me. Almost like it was a retaliation by Colton to get back at his sister for saying that there weren't swords in heaven. A little light-bulb went off in his head saying, "Yes too there are swords in heaven, and everyone makes such a big deal about what I tell them about Heaven, that I'll just tell them there are swords up there and they will believe me." <br /><br />6. And I don't believe for a single second that Colton saw Armageddon. Isn't that supposed to be a mystery when this war is supposed to take place. What would be the use of Prophets if we had little 4 year old boys telling us when it was going to occur. Once again - a little exaggerated.<br /><br />7. At two different points in the book Colton describes heaven as white &amp; gold &amp; beautiful... but then again with colors that we have never seen in this world. I just had a hard time deciding which one was true.<br /><br />Anyways - I really did think that this book was alright - there were just too many "really???"s to swallow. Like I said earlier, I believe a lot of concepts that were shared in this book - just not to the same extent that the author exploited them. Maybe my attitude would be different if I had a child which experienced Heaven at the age of 4.<br /><br />On a positive note, I did like the story about Miracles, how prayers are answered, Jesus' appearance, and miracles of tithes &amp; offerings which were shared in this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12282282631015497495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4543329669395162105">A young boy emerges from life-saving surgery with remarkable stories of his visit to heaven. <br/><br/>"Heaven Is for Real "is the true story of the four-year old son of a small town Nebraska pastor who during emergency surgery slips from consciousness and enters heaven. The family didn't know what to believe but soon the evidence was clear. <br/><br/>Colton said he met his miscarried s</span>
  <span id="freeText4543329669395162105" style="display:none">A young boy emerges from life-saving surgery with remarkable stories of his visit to heaven. <br /><br />"Heaven Is for Real "is the true story of the four-year old son of a small town Nebraska pastor who during emergency surgery slips from consciousness and enters heaven. He survives and begins talking about being able to look down and see the doctor operating and his dad praying in the waiting room. The family didn't know what to believe but soon the evidence was clear. <br /><br />Colton said he met his miscarried sister, whom no one had told him about, and his great grandfather who died 30 years before Colton was born, then shared impossible-to-know details about each. He describes the horse that only Jesus could ride, about how "reaaally big" God and his chair are, and how the Holy Spirit "shoots down power" from heaven to help us. <br /><br />Told by the father, but often in Colton's own words, the disarmingly simple message is heaven is a real place, Jesus really loves children, and be ready, there is a coming last battle.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7407872396524715898">I am not consider myself an atheist . I believe in the existence of a supreme being or beings who created this whole universe, or universes. But I am strongly oppose to the whole current as well as past rackets of Christianity .I don't care about the fact there are how many billion of people believe in this faith , because I devote my life for THE SEEKING OF TRUTH, and TRUTH ONLY regardless of how popular or unpopular , actually the more unpopular the better , of it, beside adopting other life p</span>
  <span id="freeText7407872396524715898" style="display:none">I am not consider myself an atheist . I believe in the existence of a supreme being or beings who created this whole universe, or universes. But I am strongly oppose to the whole current as well as past rackets of Christianity .I don't care about the fact there are how many billion of people believe in this faith , because I devote my life for THE SEEKING OF TRUTH, and TRUTH ONLY regardless of how popular or unpopular , actually the more unpopular the better , of it, beside adopting other life principles like beauty, nobility, love, justice ...... and a host of other life principles that are accepted and adopted by a majority if not all of us.<br /><br />Remember how unpopular it was the theory that the earth is turn around itself , not the sky and its heavenly bodies that was thought as moving around the earth ? And what has happened to the proposer ? Was his theory " crucified " by the Catholic Church ? Tell me why The Church is always , from the ancient time until now, a deformed fetus of humankind ?<br />Well then am I going to propose the bible, the foundation of Christianity is a collection of LIES ? <br />You bet.<br /><br />I am sorry if this expression of my belief is offending to those who are considering themselves Christians..But seeking the truth requires one to be brave in face of even a huge opposition from people who are unaware that they are being deceived in what I see as a whole sale brainwashing ,or from people , zombies actually in a mass hysteria as PSY 101 might have termed it. Actually, this brainwashing has been started as early as the very beginning of recorded history of mankind until the present time, and no end is coming soon.<br /><br />Who was the culprit or culprits of this brainwashing ? And what were their agenda ?<br /><br />Beside the medicine men ( healers , doctors ) ...........who pretended to know the secret of life, disease and death and weaved tons of books about it to cover their ignorance and to gain trust, awe and tribute from their unsuspecting victims, with the purpose for MATERIAL GAIN, POWER AND FAME ( beside paying student loan debt....ha ha ) ..........<br />are the high priests ( including the author of this clumsy weaving of lies) who have been doing exactly the same thing as the medicine men have been doing , namely to extract the same rewards as listed above.The only difference between this two groups of scoundrels of course is the subject mater.Naturally the high priest's "specialty " are faith, afterlife , GOD and other related subjects including the art of collecting "donation", the main source of their wealth - Who can surpass the wealth of THE Church holdings ?Perhaps not many, beside that vicious old hag who are perching in a jeweled chair at Downing St , supervising a bloody killing and looting going on right now in various parts of the world, together with her buddy , the real estate tycoon in the U S who are doing likewise."Likewise" my friends, tons of blood have spilled courtesy of the absolutely unnecessary, self-serving ( it serves very well only the noble few at the cost of blood and sweat of the mass) but most vicious "cold" war,the wars to " contain of the spread of communism" and now the' war on terror' .How many people realized, and raised a timid voice to accuse the Great Satan being the worst TERRORIST of them all ?<br /><br />Given the choices, how many among the suffering mass will shed their blood and sweat so the noble few can get a free ride of fortune, fame and power , perching in their back , holding tightly with their iron claws ? ( Iron claws you say ? Police and military together with their body guards, the gum shoes , James Bond included. Talk about Bond,it is so hard not to break out in a big laugh, ha ha ha , why ? sorry, can't elaborate here, ask G W Bush Jr. ).............................................<br /><br /> The former are the charlatans of life, the latter are the charlatans of afterlife.They are both thieves.The former use tons of medical books ( written in secret codes that only they can fathom) as their tool of their trade while the latter use the bible ( written in very old English that modern readers have to depend on 'em PRIESTS to interpret its meaning, a clever ploy to force their victims to hopelessly depend on them as "teachers")<br /><br />Now let me ask you a question.If you are God, or supreme Healer for and of mankind would you NOT "program" into his ( or her, or its) sons and daughters the wisdom of seeking help directly to HIM, HER or IT , THE SUPREME BOSS , instead of through "middle men and women" , knowing THEIR IMPERFECTIONS, their greed ,their weakness , their stupidity and evil natures ?(Remember the extreme evil Popes of yesteryears and the sexual predators among the priests of this modern time ?).<br /><br />In the case of Buddhism, it is much more frightening .It has thousands of thick volumes of "Buddha teaching" , written in Sanskrit or other ancient languages that are absolutely maddening .Nobody but the very few among the most "venerable " monks can understand its meaning.The devotees have no choice but obligate to thankfully accept morsels of "Buddha Teaching" the high monks dispense , if they want a ticket for the Nirvana .Of course the prize goes to the higher bidders !<br /><br />Heaven, anyone ?<br /><br />It is not even funny, it is sickening !<br /><br />Now if you are God, or Buddha, or Supreme Being,being the most compassionate one, would you NOT make the knowledge of life and afterlife AS SIMPLE, AS EASY TO UNDERSTAND FOR A TEN YEAR OLD CHILD .? <br /><br />If you ask any ten year old child about religion, he or she will tell you , in his or her simple language of a child his /her age, that IF YOU DO GOOD, YOU GO TO HEAVEN. Isn't it absolutely beautiful , simple,truthful and complete ? Do you need Sunday bible classes and masses , Bible colleges, foam mouthed priests, frenzy pastors or thousand of volumes of "Buddha Teaching" together with human decoders, the most venerable Big Ass Monks ?<br /><br />It make you sick, really sick.How can you make a joke about this madness ?<br /><br /><br /> Here is one example.We all know the father of western healing art , Hippocrates, right ?.What was his "teaching " ? Extremely simple :.LET 'S FOOD BE YOUR MEDICINE, LET'S MEDICINE BE YOUR FOOD, or something to that effect. ISN'T IT BEAUTIFUL , WHOLESOME, SIMPLE AND COMPLETE ?.Do you need to push a guy, or gal for that mater, through 10 plus years of medical college to be able to follow the footsteps of Hippocrates ? ( Of course excluding medical tech guys and gals in various specialty like dental, mental, surgical,ob......etc) Would five minutes will do ( Of course emergency med,surgical , physical and psychological therapy and some others excluded , and required proper training )<br /><br />Can you see ? They weave tons of unnecessary and bogus "knowledge" and ritual to create a needed myth , a needed halo around the medicine men and women and their colleagues , the high priests to create the respectability for them and to earn awe and submission from their preys, the mass, who will understandably too eager , too willing to open their pocket for these "savior", middle men and women of God , or in the case of medicine, God of Healing.<br /><br />GOD INC. ! Their wealth is staggering !<br /><br />They created the bogus "knowledge" for the noble few, who then dispense this "knowledge" depending the tribute they receive.This mountain of "knowledge" contained in thousands of books of all kinds hardly bring people any closer to improve human health .Even though average life span has extended considerably, man still be besieged with uncountable afflictions that modern medicines are nothing but temporary reliefs.<br /><br />I am not discounting the knowledge of human anatomy , it is absolutely needed for surgeons and physical therapists.But the rest, tons of book about human health and diseases did not bring human any closer to improve their health.Quite oppositely, it serves only as tool of the money making trade , and actually are making human health going from bad to worst with their extremely toxic and injurious chemicals they called medicines and their total disregard about the effect of the tremendous toxic chemicals used in the production of food and drink .What is their reason for acting like that ? Because, DOING OTHERWISE WILL NOT MAKING THEM RICH.Talk about the evilness of money !<br />Health care and Heaven must never be for sale <br /><br />You can find the VOW OF POVERTY, THE MOST NOBLE VIRTUE OF "ANCIENT" MEN , only in museum !<br /><br />Any Truth that can't be explain to a ten year old child is not worth knowing and is a menace to mankind.Even in the collection of lies you can find some rare gems.Remember what Jesus told his devotees ? Let's the children come to me.Children, c h i l d r e n , my friends.<br /><br />THERE IS A CLEAR CONFLICT OF INTEREST HERE, the healer 's purpose of a business transaction is to MAKE MONEY,and therefor, the longer the therapy the better.It goes directly against the purpose of their preys, the patients, who are just want to restore their health to prior condition AS SOON AS POSSIBLE.<br /><br />iT IS undeniable the fact that the healer 's subconscious wish directly affect the outcome of his therapeutic maneuver upon his patient.It is very sad, the current situation where the healer , lost her sacred, but outdated virtue ( selfless love ) of a mother hen toward her chicks , her patients , as in the olden time, has LOST ALSO THE EFFECT OF HER THERAPEUTIC MAGIC , a very important component of treatment, that existed in the long lost past.<br /><br />ANY WONDER THE DISASTROUS and dismal CURRENT SITUATION OF HEALTH and HEALTHCARE ?<br /><br />'EM HEALERS don't give a rat's ass about that dead old man Hippocrates , even though they just took his OATH not long ago.Gotta make money baby.<br /><br />I say to you, dear readers and fellow book reviewers : GET RID OF 'EM MEDICINE MEN and WOMEN together with 'EM HIGH PRIESTS, including and especially the HALF-GOD who are siting in his gilded throne inside that ROME'S glorious castle ( don't you impress by the big ass crowd of devotees they drawn, 'em zombies,) and of course that " REAL " GOD ,the globe trotting , the pretending amicable Dalai Latma .'EM SCOUNDRELS .<br /><br />WHAT ARE THIS MAD CROWD WORSHIPING ? 'EM IMPOSTOR OF GOD (OR BUDDHA) , or the actual, THE REAL GOD ( OR BUDDHA ) HIMSELF , HERSELF or itself ?<br /><br />LET PEOPLE GO DIRECTLY TO THEIR GODS, WHOEVER OR WHATEVER MAY BE, at low cost, or no cost at all.How much does it cost, in term of money , time &amp; energy to pray whenever &amp; wherever you feel like. <br />Let educate people from kindergarten up about Hippocrates ' simple teaching or that of HAI THUONG LAN ONG, or whoever health teacher of old may be, and let the people keep themselves healthy through proper diet and other sanitary habit without the extremely expensive , potential injurious "medicine" ( non food chemicals).I believe- without millions of dollar to perform "researches" to "prove"- that one of modern incurable diseases, the AIDS , is direct result of monster viruses who defy all medicines, created BY , MOST UNFORTUNATELY , and courtesy of extreme abusing use of vast number of various antibiotics and a host of other extremely toxic "medicine". Hippocrates would turn in his grave !<br /><br />I am hesitate to extol the elimination of all doctors.Perhaps we still need emergency rooms ,emergency medicines , physical and psychological therapy , surgery , dentistry and few other specialties but let get rid of the rest.<br /><br />Return to religion.<br /><br />What is the foundation of my theory? Can I prove the Bible is a collection of lies, cleverly weaved by , I have to admit , very bright, very intelligent( but gold mad ) men and not surprisingly NOT WOMEN. (More about it later, if I have time and space)<br /><br />Let me tell you a story.One day I encountered a college student in the street, with a bible clutching in his hand.He was very nice both in appearance and demeanor, very pleasant conversant.Unfortunately he has tried to enlist a wrong person to the vicious Crusade where he was one of its foot soldier , sorry fella.<br /><br />I removed my left shoe and sock , pointed to my toe nails, and asked him.Do you know what is the function of these nails ?After a long pause, he admitted he didn't know.HA ! CAN YOU BELIEVE IT ? A COLLEGE student, no less, and didn't know the function of the toe nails !<br /><br />But , can you blame him ?Remember, he was , like thousands if not millions of his contemporaries, is being educated by the ESTABLISHMENT. I am not discounting the tremendous knowledge the school are trying to help him to obtain.But as the ESTABLISHMENT, it falls under the control of the noble few whose agenda , whose mind is set in concrete , i e to protect and further their own social class 's interest.Therefore, they brainwashing 'em with half-truths and lies beside real knowledge with the purpose to turn him into one of their Crusade's foot soldier.<br /><br />Have you ever wonder, when you trimmed your toe nails , what is the purpose of God, if there is one, when He created the nails for the toes ?<br /><br />Ha, you flunk this biology and religion test !<br /><br />Well my friends, millions ,billions of years ago, the toes nail were very essential for the survival of the then human -like species.You see, you can not climb very effectively without 'em.THIS IS NOT FAITH MY FRIENDS, IT IS SCIENCE,Even though it still has a lot of missing links, but the theory of creationism has NO LINK AT ALL <br /><br />THEN for whatever reasons you walked upright. Perhaps courtesy of the environment changes: The jungle gave way to savanna. Walking upright instead of moving in all fours, gave our distant ancestor a life and death advantage of seeing above the grass and brush levels.Especially if your meddlesome in -laws had a habit of always coming unannounced!<br />Or perhaps because it was more dignifying ? Just imagine the politicians of this modern day move in all fours, or worse, climb a poll in the House and Senate, or Kennedy climbed a tree to pursue M M ( of course you know it stands for Marilyn Monroe.Heaven rest you lovely soul ,countenance and body . Despite many smart remarks about you, my dear , you have more brain than that scoundrel .)<br />Ah , Kennedy ! America is perhaps one of very few countries in the world that name a murderer to a geographic area AND an airport.The crime scene is sanitized but it can't wiped out the fact that this despicable womanizer has murdered his one time bed partner to silence her after she threatened to scandalize their affair.<br /><br />How about replace the Liberty Lady with the statue of Kennedy holding high a loaded CYRINGE ?And what about the inscription in its base ? DON'T TREAD ON ME BABY ? or DON'T ........... WITH ME BABY ?<br /><br />THE THEORY OF CREATIONISM IS FOR THE BIRDS ( together with high priests}, it can't apply for monkeys or other primates and actually for any living organism, and lastly absolutely NOT for man.<br /><br />There goes into the dust bin, the Bible<br /><br />Extremely sad though, it will not, and never be made to disappear forever..It will stand there for a foreseeable future , causing more bloodshed and suffering (Crusade of yesteryears , war on "terror "and the "cold war" of this modern time) while it enriching the top 1 percent of one percent of world population, the like of Obama , Trump and their predecessors together with their cohort and big industrialist providers and protectors,'em king makers and the indispensable LOBBYISTS , the most dirty appendage of the most dirty trick they call "democracy"<br /><br />There are many proofs of Darwinism.<br /><br />One of it is the extreme similarity between the DNA of chimps and human.No similarity can be found among all other species.This is extremely important considering the tremendous number of animal species.<br /><br />The discovery of prehistoric primate and human-like skulls and skeletons that , even with "missing links" , shows an undeniable progression toward the modern human form from the more crude forms.<br />It is so embarrassing to joke about THE ARK . How many set of boys and girls, 'em DINOSAUERs , can be thrown into the very crowded ship ?As their size is enormous, how many of 'em dino's can be put into just ONE Ark ? Three ? Then how many Noah 's Ark is needed to save just 'em dino's alone ? Especially they by nature like to roam.?Perhaps inject them with some barbiturates .? But then you need many other ARKS to fit all of 'em animals . A boon to shipbuilders of ancient time !<br /><br />The last argument against the Bible is the diet of meat that modern human being is adopting.Now, it is very clear , among all scientists, that based on the human anatomy, from the intestine ( short for meat-eating animals, long for vegetable -eating animals) , the teeth ( sharp for the FORMER , dull for the latter) , locomotion ( fast for the former, slow for the latter ), claws (sharp for the former and dull for the latter ) HUMAN SPECIES IS INDISPUTABLY belong to the latter, the herbivorous animal, not the carnivorous !<br /> <br />Then why was all of this business about God had given man the role of the "manager" of all species of animal that inhabit the earth , implying to kill and consume their meats ?<br /><br />Clearly whoever or whatever that created human beings, he, she or it DID NOT INTEND their diet to include meat.<br /><br /> .It is not funny anymore, it is sickening to think of the vast destruction courtesy of this collection of fantasies they call the word of God.<br />Yes, may be the heaven is for real, but not as this book or the bible proposes.<br /><br /><br />POST SCRIPT<br /><br />After I finished the above writing, in a conversation between I and a lady of Muslim faith, in answer to me about her celebrating or memorizing and honoring the death of Jesus Christ, she dismissed the concept of J C altogether.Due to the limitation of her English speaking ability , she could not elaborate, but I could gain a peek of what she was trying to say.<br />Then it dawned on me , I am being right all along in this thesis.J C was after all just a clever creation of the ancient nobles, together with his words, the Bible.<br />Why should God, whoever or whatever may be , USED A HUMAN BEING TO CARRY HIS MESSAGE TO HIS CHILDREN ?<br />Why shouldn't HIS CREATION, HIS CHILDREN have the ability to be inspired by the wonder of the universe and communicate directly with its creator or creators by themselves without the human money changers ?<br /><br />Why shouldn't they by pass any human "representatives" no mater who they claim they are, J C included.Here is the truth : How many man of the cloth, sitting behind the screen of the "confession booth" , can resist the urge of peeking through it, if the confessor is an attractive girl, and further, NOT have a hard on or worse, grab or ....................her ( as it happened enough time to such extend that the HALF GOD , THE POPE had to cried in shame and anger of his charges' weakness and criminal acts against their parishioners ]<br /><br /> Friends , tell your wife, daughter or girlfriend to just confess and ask forgiveness directly to their God, whoever OR whatever they believe in, at whatever time and place they desire.<br /><br />With due respect to the people faiths and religious beliefs, as sacred and dear to their hearts as they should be, I think the Bible , with so many holes , as described above, WAS JUST A HUMAN CREATION.As many of other human creations,however clever it is, it bear holes.<br /><br /><br />GOD CREATION BEARS NO HOLES .<br /><br />It was created ........., I am sorry to repeat myself once more ,to satisfy the human , in this case, the noble few,........... to be able to perch on a grand pedestal of fame, nobility , respectability, and last but not least power and fortune.<br /><br />In the process, it creates untold miseries !<br /><br />HOW DARE ANY HUMAN BEINGS , JC INCLUDED IF IN FACT JC WAS A REAL HISTORICAL PERSON, WHO HAS THE AUDACITY TO STAND GUARD AT THE GATE OF HEAVEN AND DECLARES NO ONE CAN ENTER UNLESS GETTING A NOD FROM HIM OR HER except God himself ?<br /><br />INDEED, HOW DARE !</span>

I find his God too small, but perhaps God tailored the boy's heaven experience specifically to him. We'll know when we get there!</span>

<div id="review_888764083" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/888764083" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/888764083?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781608147915" href="/book/show/13428394-heaven-is-for-real">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer888764083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1400577675671977725">I'm not putting this on any shelf other than "read". I'm not going to take a stand on any other heading.<br/><br/>The first part of this book was hard for me to read, I suppose it will be for most parents. Knowing we're closing in on an account of either the near death or temporary death of a child will bear down on anyone who has children. <br/><br/>After that we get into the account of "how the parents came to believe that their child had been conscious in Heaven". The point of the book is that Colton remembered </span>
  <span id="freeText1400577675671977725" style="display:none">I'm not putting this on any shelf other than "read". I'm not going to take a stand on any other heading.<br /><br />The first part of this book was hard for me to read, I suppose it will be for most parents. Knowing we're closing in on an account of either the near death or temporary death of a child will bear down on anyone who has children. <br /><br />After that we get into the account of "how the parents came to believe that their child had been conscious in Heaven". The point of the book is that Colton remembered seeing Jesus and sitting on his lap (not far fetched at all as Christ showed love for children when on earth and speaks of love for children). Colton also expresses other memories of his stay in Heaven which include descriptions of how things look and so on. <br /><br />Some people have accused the parents of being exploitative with this book...I WILL NOT go there. There is no evidence of that that I saw. If it's true it's between them and God (well and Colton). So assuming they are sincere in the writing where do we go?<br /><br />Well critics have pointed out that some of the things seen seem to be unbiblical. I can see their point. Some of the descriptions given by Colton do raise questions about the state of those already in Heave. But then this is a little boy. If he indeed does remember an encounter with Christ Jesus I'm sure Jesus would have presented things to him in a way easy for a child to understand. I'm not willing to quibble over whether Christians "in Heaven" have wings. Nor do I feel like arguing over soul sleep or other critical ideas raised by those looking for detail problems. If Jesus did deal with a child He would have dealt with him in a way the child could understand.<br /><br />Did Colton have an experience in heaven he remembers? I don't know. Some find this book inspiring others not. I certainly won't nay say it. Try it yourself, see what you think. I didn't enjoy it as it's about a child who was injured. Past that are questions. I'm a Christian and I don't doubt that if God wanted this it would be...is it a real account. As noted, I don't know, however God does. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1400577675671977725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5KLYncT6NdBzcuJka8P48sHEOPBra0MzQ3zolQ07Inq9vIZ7LjvYca+7yO/wOJvf2OlK0tr/zJT/Y9LoNpxcCQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

like.\n\nFeatures include:\n\n\n5 sessions of study for group members\nFor use with DVD sessions (ISBN 9781418550660)\nConversation Guide written for both believers and non-believers in accessible
